<div id="review_183750458" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183750458" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183750458?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Hourglass Door, or even those who wanted more out of Existence</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=general-fantasy-and-mythology">general-fantasy-and-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=hybrid-multiple-genre">hybrid-multiple-genre</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183750458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15185589690750250295"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>
      <s>Needs More Mythology</s>
    </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I figured that was going to be my review opener until I hit the last portion of the book. The connection between the realm of the gods and our world wasn't made clear upfront, but wouldn't you know...the author had to sneak some of it in on us at the last minute.<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Buried alive...</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Nikki (Becks) is back in town after a long period of time away. 100 years underground, to be exact. Yet, in everyone else's perspective, they think she's only been go</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15185589690750250295" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>
      <s>Needs More Mythology</s>
    </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I figured that was going to be my review opener until I hit the last portion of the book. The connection between the realm of the gods and our world wasn't made clear upfront, but wouldn't you know...the author had to sneak some of it in on us at the last minute.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Buried alive...</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Nikki (Becks) is back in town after a long period of time away. 100 years underground, to be exact. Yet, in everyone else's perspective, they think she's only been gone a matter of months. When heartache caused Nikki to bargain for time in the Everneath as a way to cope with the pain, she was forced to pay the price - one which might not come with an 'out clause'. Is it possible for her to regain her life at all, now that she's living on borrowed time?</i> <br><br>This is another case of a story which had good bones, but suffered from a little bit of a deficiency when it came to character depth. No one in this story truly grabbed me, other than Cole (of course it would figure that I'd be curious about the presumed villain). I feel somewhat guilty that the characters of Jack and Cole kept making me think of Dank and Leif from the <i>Existence</i> trilogy, because this was a huge hurdle for me to get over, considering how I wasn't a big fan of Existence. Jack was a combination of the old boyfriend and Dank, while Cole was Leif (although the rock star thing was switched, with the villain being the musician this time). However, in the case of <i>Everneath</i>, the story had a touch more finesse. Even if you weren't a fan of <i>Existence</i>, you might still be able to find something to enjoy about <i>Everneath.</i><br><br>Although it took me almost an entire book to warm up to Jack, the last scene with him at the end of the book melted my heart and appealed to the romantic in me. But wouldn't it figure that of course I'm hopelessly and recklessly vibing on Cole instead. I know it's wrong, but I can't help it!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You don't give my job enough credit. It's really hard to convince a girl to follow me. The average pickup lines don't work so well. 'Hey, wanna get coffee? And then spend an eternity getting the life force sucked out of you?' They don't go for it."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Aww hell, Nikki. I may not get why you did what you did, but at least you made me think of Charlie Sheen with this gem : <i>One day is all I deserve, and I've had so many already. I've won. I've won!</i> I had the urge to put up one of his "DUH WINNING" pics but then I saw this and felt it appropriate for the story :<br><span>[image error]</span><br>I'm guessing that's about how Nikki looked after being drained of energy, too. <br><br>Surprisingly enough, I was okay with the back-and-forth timeline. In this particular case, the "waiting" to find certain things out sort of lent an air of mystery to the book. The author had a way of bringing us between the past and the present with little loss of cohesion. There is a fair amount of skill involved in doing this without confusing the readers. I'll give a thumbs up for that.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Where do we go from here?"<br>"Nowhere, really," I whispered. "it doesn't change anything."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I wasn't in love with the story but I was in like with the ideas presented. Because there was a great buildup to finding out some answers while still leaving many things a mystery for now, this ended up being the factor which had me wanting to keep reading. Even when I wasn't completely attaching to the characters, I was fascinated with the idea of what was to come. The end of the book is where the story finally hit an AHAH! moment for me. Then I had an <i>oh hell yeah, I can't wait to see what happens next</i> feeling. I'm happy that book 2 is just around the corner now because I have to believe that we're on our way up to the top of the roller-coaster now, just about to plunge over that cliff. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The pain of loss was fresh every night, but I no longer begged to have it taken away. I owned it.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15185589690750250295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_299694826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/299694826" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/299694826?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-want-it-right-now">i-want-it-right-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=almost-fell-asleep">almost-fell-asleep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=caught-in-a-bad-romance">caught-in-a-bad-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=clever-plot-twists">clever-plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=deserves-the-hype">deserves-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=didn-t-see-that-coming">didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer299694826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17326387979858941320">Actual Rating: 2.5 stars<br/><br/><i>Everneath</i> is one of those books that seems to be followed by hype everywhere it goes, and, for the most part, understandably so. <i>Everneath</i> is an overall compelling, captivating, and at times heartbreaking read, truly worthy of the hype it has undoubtedly gotten. <br/><br/>But just because I see where the hype is coming from concerning <i>Everneath</i> doesn't necessarily mean I'm taking part in it. <br/><br/>Conceptually, <i>Everneath</i> is practically flawless; a loose retelling of the myths of Persepho</span>
  <span id="freeText17326387979858941320" style="display:none">Actual Rating: 2.5 stars<br /><br /><i>Everneath</i> is one of those books that seems to be followed by hype everywhere it goes, and, for the most part, understandably so. <i>Everneath</i> is an overall compelling, captivating, and at times heartbreaking read, truly worthy of the hype it has undoubtedly gotten. <br /><br />But just because I see where the hype is coming from concerning <i>Everneath</i> doesn't necessarily mean I'm taking part in it. <br /><br />Conceptually, <i>Everneath</i> is practically flawless; a loose retelling of the myths of Persephone and Eurydice, where teenager Nikki Beckett is sucked into an underworld known the inhabitants as the Everneath and lives there for hundreds of years, only to return to the real world and discover six months has passed. But this time, Nicki has only six more months to redeem her mysterious disappearance, apologize to the loved ones she left - including her old boyfriend, Jack, and ultimately, say good-bye to them one last time, as her clock is ticking and the Everneath is ready to claim her again. <br /><br />But, however, it's with the execution of the above concept where I feel <i>Everneath</i> went wrong. Brodi Ashton could have gone so much farther with the thoroughly interesting mythology presented to us in the synopsis, but unfortunately, the most mythology in the entirety of <i>Everneath</i> is in the opening chapters, and the final few chapters. <br /><br />The chapters in between the opening few and the final few are filled with an excruciatingly boring romance and tons of relationship angst, and just angst in general. While others may tell you that <i>Everneath</i> is focused on a teenager searching for redemption after disappearing mysteriously from her loved one's lives, I would tell you that <i>Everneath</i> is mostly about Nikki's attempts at rebuilding her past relationships - most prominently her relationship with her former boyfriend, Jack. <br /><br />Jack is another reason I went into <i>Everneath</i> with extremely high expectations, after seeing so many reviews praising him and comparing him to the likes of Tucker Avery - a character I'm pretty sure <i>everybody</i> loves, but throughout the entirety of <i>Everneath</i>, I never found myself feeling more than dismissive towards him. While I found him to be a kind and sweet character, I also found him to be just as bland as Nikki. In fact, I think it's safe to say that I liked Nikki's captor of sorts, Cole, much more than Jack. While Cole wasn't a love interest in <i>Everneath</i>, I can definitely tell that he is going to end up being one in <i>Everbound</i>, and I'm actually really glad. Unlike the characters of Nikki and Jack, I found Cole to be multi-layered, interesting, and bearing the correlation of a real human being, whereas I found Nikki and Jack to be overall one-dimensional and boring. <br /><br /> Another thing to be noted about <i>Everneath</i> is that a suspension of disbelief is pretty much a necessity if you plan on reading it. After her disappearance, Nikki's father obviously asks her where she's been for the past six months, and once Nikki answers him with, "Oh, just rehab." (paraphrasing, of course, but this is pretty much what happened), her father completely lets go of the issue as if that was a good enough answer. I also find it incredibly implausible that Jack would be so accepting of Nikki's story about where she really was over the past six months, when any other person would have (and <i>should</i> have) stared at her and sent her to a psychiatric ward. <br /><br />And while I have mostly negative feelings towards <i>Everneath</i>, none of those feelings are particularly strong or passionate - I didn't hate it, I didn't like it, and I wouldn't even say I'm somewhere in the middle of like and hate. In the end, I was left with just an overall feeling of meh, whether it be concerning the execution of the plot, the romance, the characters, or the writing. Just meh, and honestly, I think that might just be the worst feeling I could have for a book. When I hate a book, at least I'm able to say that the book drew some emotion from me, but when I'm left with an overall feeling meh and dismissiveness, I'm unable to say I felt anything. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17326387979858941320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_232459772" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/232459772" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232459772?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Vinaya by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-liked">books-i-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=fluff-fluffy-fluffest">fluff-fluffy-fluffest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=mixed-vibes">mixed-vibes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232459772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9634029227725831263"><i>"That night, when I left the dorm, I could have gone home and shut myself in my room. I could've faced you and yelled at you. But I didn't. I took the easy way out. I begged for the easy way out. Cole took the pain away and I didn't care that it would ruin everything in my life, because I was stupid enough to think I had nothing else to lose."</i><br/><br/>I admit I'm a fairly preachy reviewer, in general. I like to lecture my authors on how to send the 'right' messages, and how to avoid being paranormal clic</span>
  <span id="freeText9634029227725831263" style="display:none"><i>"That night, when I left the dorm, I could have gone home and shut myself in my room. I could've faced you and yelled at you. But I didn't. I took the easy way out. I begged for the easy way out. Cole took the pain away and I didn't care that it would ruin everything in my life, because I was stupid enough to think I had nothing else to lose."</i><br /><br />I admit I'm a fairly preachy reviewer, in general. I like to lecture my authors on how to send the 'right' messages, and how to avoid being paranormal clichés, and how to build healthy relationships. But at the base of it all, I pan books when they're not entertaining enough. When my entertainment comes with a dose of perceptiveness and good writing and life-positive messages, I am super-extra happy, but I have been known to love books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10118172.Spellbound__Spellbound___1_" title="Spellbound (Spellbound, #1) by Cara Lynn Shultz" rel="nofollow noopener">Spellbound</a> simply for the entertainment quotient. *blushes*<br /><br />Everneath probably doesn't deserve the fourth star. But it was interesting and kept me entertained the whole way through, and the good definitely hugely outweighed the bad, so I'm willing to forgive it its faults. First off, let me tell you, I LOVE the take Brody Ashton took on the Hades-Persephone myth. It might quite possibly be the most interesting retelling of the myth I've read in YA, and considering the number of retellings floating around out there, that's really saying something. So Nikki Beckett finds out, to her detriment, that Hades (Everneath) is not really the world of the dead, but instead a place for immortals, called the Everliving, who sustain themselves by feeding off willing human sacrifices. In a moment of madness, Nikki offers herself up to one of the Everliving, and emerges six months later wispy and drained out, but with her memories and self strangely intact. She knows her time on earth is numbered - in six months she will have to choose between becoming Everliving herself or becoming food for the shades that haunt Everneath, but in the meantime, she is determined to do her best this time around and settle her affairs, so to speak, before she vanishes for good. <br /><br />I liked Nikki. As Kat says in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231306350" rel="nofollow noopener">her review</a>, Nikki is like a drug addict fighting to rise above her addiction. The connection between her and Cole (the immortal who fed on her) is very different from the feelings she has for Jack, the boy she left behind. With Cole, there is no depth of feeling, or shared history or sharp pain. She looks at Cole the way an alcoholic would study a bootle of Jack - with a mixture of loathing and desire. And, as the quote above shows, she's not afraid to stand up and admit her faults. Since the book splits the narrative between the present time, and her life before the Feed, it's easy to see how much more mature the returned Nikki Beckett is. <br /><br />Jack, on the other hand, is the quintessential sweetheart - with a dash of edge, as evinced by his eyebrow piercing. He's in love with Nikki, always has been, and while this <i>could</i> have been a cop-out in terms of romantic characterization, it doesn't feel that way. Jack's sweet and steadfast, and I really liked the way he wooed her back out of her shell. He's more of a Tucker boy than an Edward boy and we all know which one I prefer!<br /><br />But, of course, this book is not perfect. I found the idea of the Daughters of Persephone weird and unconvincing. I can see a few crazy people selling off their daughters for a vague promise of immortality. But entire societies of them? All over the world? Really?<br /><br />More importantly (and annoyingly) Ashton falls into that most common of YA tropes, the Disappearing Parent Syndrome. Nikki disappears for six months, <i>
  <b>nobody</b>
</i> has the faintest idea where she's been, she emerges emaciated and withdrawn, and her father's only response is to bring a random woman home to test her for drugs, and then leave her by herself for long stretches of time? Please. There is no mention of her father frantically searching for her - Jack, sure, Jack never gave up, but apparently the man who gave life to her was willing to consign his daughter to the recesses of his mind and move on with his life. He never takes her to the shrink, he doesn't hover constantly and check on where she is, and when she gets caught in the middle of a fight, his only response is to worry about his campaign for mayor... and yet we are supposed to believe he is a loving father. That does not play for me at all. <br /><br />Nikki too treats her family with cavalier disregard. Although she mentions over and over again that she came back to settle things with her dad and say goodbye to her little brother, except for one obligatory scene with both of them, we never see her actually spending time with her family, making her brother feel better, even <i>thinking</i> about him all that much. It's all me-me-me-Jack-Jack-Jack. Even her so-called best friend, Jules, get the short shrift. Now I was a teenager once, and I DID spend more time dramatizing my lovelife and ignoring my parents - when I wasn't hating on them, that is. BUT, I had not just returned from a life-changing experience, and I was not expecting to die in the next six months. You'd think that sort of thing would change a person's perspective. <br /><br />But all in all, this was a pretty interesting book, there was enough interesting things happening that the annoying things didn't annoy me too much. If you don't like the general run of YA PNRs, I would suggest you stay away from Everneath, but if you like the genre in general and don't mind a certain amount of genre conformity in your YA books, then give this one a shot. <br /><br /><i>This book was provided by the publisher via Net Galley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9634029227725831263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9730275757711548272"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/brodi-ashton/review-everneath.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352252i/705752.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
</a><br/><br/>There might be times in your life when you feel that you’ve hit the very bottom and that you can’t take it anymore.<br/>Try to imagine for a moment that you have lost everything you care about. That someone would tell you that it’s in his power to take all your pain away.. What would you do? Would you take the chance?<br/><br/>You might say “no”, you might say “maybe” or even you might agree..<br/>But what if it is not only the pain that it’s taken away from you, what if you’re fading away with every memo</span>
  <span id="freeText9730275757711548272" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/brodi-ashton/review-everneath.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352252i/705752.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
</a><br><br>There might be times in your life when you feel that you’ve hit the very bottom and that you can’t take it anymore.<br>Try to imagine for a moment that you have lost everything you care about. That someone would tell you that it’s in his power to take all your pain away.. What would you do? Would you take the chance?<br><br>You might say “no”, you might say “maybe” or even you might agree..<br>But what if it is not only the pain that it’s taken away from you, what if you’re fading away with every memory, with every beat of your heart, with every second until there is nothing but void… you turn to nothing (even with the promise of immortality)<br><br>What memory do you think you could keep hidden in your heart to wake you to life, to call for you when you’re lost?<br>Would it be about your family, or friends, or a lover?<br>Will it be a face, a smile, a happy moment?..<br><br><a href="http://hanachan732.deviantart.com/art/The-Embrace-85530634" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352252i/705753._SY540_.jpg" alt="" width="241" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Nikki has lost what she thought that it was ‘everything’ for her and she has decided that she doesn’t want to feel the pain any longer. She has given herself away (when a boy called Cole told her that he can erase all her suffering), now she has no feelings, her memory is back in pieces, and she has a few months to say goodbye to the people she cares about and then she will disappear from this world for ever.<br>The only thing she recalls is the face of a boy, her first love, and one of her big disappointments – Jack.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Every breath I took meant another grain of sand in my hourglass disappeared, and I only had a few left. I tried not breathing.</i>
</blockquote><br>With the time ticking her life away she doesn’t have many choices.<br>It all sounds simple: say goodbye to Jack, to her father and her brother. She thinks that she has enough time to prepare herself, to say how sorry she is, to leave it all behind. But simple is just a word, and life is never simple.<br><br>…Now old friends come back from the past, misunderstandings are revealed, Nikki’s heart starts to feel again, but all the love in the world is not enough to protect her, to keep her for disappearing again.<br>Her only chance is to use all the time she has to find a way to cheat “fate”; her only chance is to get Cole to tell her what could she do to break the unbreakable, but would he do that for her, or even could he?<br><br>I liked how she doubted Cole from time to time, but then her doubts would vanish and the numbness would return again. I liked how she and Jake got to become close again, day by day, how she remembered more of their moments together (oh, how I liked the sparks of life from the memories) and I liked how Jake wouldn’t give up on her no matter what.<br>They were cute together and my heart was breaking with every chapter seeing how little time they had together and how much of it did they waste.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352252i/705754.jpg" alt="" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also Cole was quite a mystery, and one that I would want to uncover. He was fun to be around and if it wasn’t for the fact that he was sucking feelings out of people I might have liked him a lot better.<br><br>So, if you like paranormal stories with a touch of mythology and some interesting characters, this is your chance. I hope that you will enjoy it as much as I did.<br><br><i>Book Source: ARC from the publisher via Netgalley – Thank you very much!</i><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/brodi-ashton/review-everneath.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/brodi-ashton/review-everneath.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

<div id="review_201154669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201154669" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201154669?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062071156" href="/book/show/12127178-everneath">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Paranormal Romance Fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=netgalley-e-book">netgalley-e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201154669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9078837854204758678">I couldn’t stop thinking about this book after I was done reading it. It was haunting, and heart-breaking….and I loved it.<br/><br/>Seventeen-year old Nikki Bennett, Becks, has been gone for six months in the Everneath, a place where Everlivings, immortal beings, feed off the emotions of humans to survive. Nikki has come home to say a proper good-bye to her family and friends, most of all a proper good-bye to Jack, the love of her life. Nikki has six months on the surface before the Everneath claims her f</span>
  <span id="freeText9078837854204758678" style="display:none">I couldn’t stop thinking about this book after I was done reading it. It was haunting, and heart-breaking….and I loved it.<br /><br />Seventeen-year old Nikki Bennett, Becks, has been gone for six months in the Everneath, a place where Everlivings, immortal beings, feed off the emotions of humans to survive. Nikki has come home to say a proper good-bye to her family and friends, most of all a proper good-bye to Jack, the love of her life. Nikki has six months on the surface before the Everneath claims her for good to serve either as a “battery” in the dark tunnels or to become an Everliving with Cole, the Everliving who took her. At first you know that Nikki made the choice willingly to go with Cole, but you don’t know why. You get glimpses of the past events that led up to her decision, throughout the story. You know that her mother died in a car accident and that she’s devastated about that. However, Nikki also has other things going for her, like Jack. Jack was her best-friend that she secretly loved for many years, until they figured out their feelings were mutual. In flash-backs you see that Nikki has some doubts of her worth to Jack, and some problems with her family. Cole takes advantage of that, encouraging her doubt. Everlivings entice people in pain, because The Feed takes all those emotions away. Unfortunately, The Feed also takes every emotion you have away, leaving you an empty shell. Now Nikki would do anything to change the bargain she made with Cole. <br /><br />This story made my heart <i>ache</i> for Nikki and Jack. It felt like I was watching someone tying up loose ends before a death sentence! It pained me to see Nikki realizing how close her best-friend, Jules and Jack became after she disappeared, and feeling the jealousy she felt because of it. Jack, though, is such an unwavering, persistent guy, never giving up on Nikki while she was gone or now, when she’s back. Their romance is so <i>very</i> sweet, although mainly told from flash-backs. Loved this scene: <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“You weren’t in the lunchroom today.” Jack said, coming up behind me at my locker. “Jules says you’re never in the cafeteria on Wednesdays.” I tried to calm the flush to my cheeks before I turned around to face him. My crush on Jack was getting ridiculous….Just because he noticed, for the first time, that I wasn’t at lunch, it didn’t mean anything…. ”She said you avoid the cafeteria on Wednesdays. And she said you like me.” I heard myself gasp, and I came to a stop. “So is it true?” Jack said….I turned away, embarrassed, but Jack stepped sideways so he was in front of me, and there was nowhere else I could look. “Yes. I hate hot-dog Wednesdays, so I don’t go to the lunchroom. It’s true.” Jack: “That’s not what I meant, Becks.” Nikki: “I know.” Jack: “Tell me. Is it true? Do you like me?” Nikki: “You know I like you. You’re one of my best friends.” Jack: “Friends.” Nikki: “Of course.” Jack: “Good friends?” Nikki: I nodded. Jack: “More than friends?” Nikki: I didn’t say anything. I didn’t move. Jack reached toward my hand and tugged gently on my fingers. He leaned forward and said, “Tell me, friend. Is there more for us?” Nikki: I looked down at my feet. “There’s everything for us.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Oh, how you want them to find a way around this mess! <br /><br />I liked that this story incorporates an original take on Greek Mythology, the story of Hades and the Underworld twisted up a bit. I hope that’s developed more in the next one. And the ending!!! Oh, the ending!! I can’t wait to see what happens next. A definite recommend!<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Harper Collins and Netgalley for allowing me to read this!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9078837854204758678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_799079258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/799079258" />
    <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews"><img alt="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468898958p2/12502667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/799079258?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews">Rachel  (APCB Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer799079258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7819428148036300204">Summary of Review Below: Fan-freaking-tastic!!<br/><br/>Nikki was drawn to the Everneath by Cole. When Nikki was in the Everneath the only memories she retained were those of her boyfriend Jack. By some miraculous miracle, Nikki survives the feeding in the Everneath and returns to the Surface six months after disappearing just to see Jack again. Nikki tries to put back together the pieces of her shattered life and make her final goodbyes before the Tunnels capture her for good. <br/><br/>This gif sums up my feeling</span>
  <span id="freeText7819428148036300204" style="display:none">Summary of Review Below: Fan-freaking-tastic!!<br><br>Nikki was drawn to the Everneath by Cole. When Nikki was in the Everneath the only memories she retained were those of her boyfriend Jack. By some miraculous miracle, Nikki survives the feeding in the Everneath and returns to the Surface six months after disappearing just to see Jack again. Nikki tries to put back together the pieces of her shattered life and make her final goodbyes before the Tunnels capture her for good. <br><br>This gif sums up my feelings towards this book pretty well:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389317473ra/8019614.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I LOVED this book. I was intrigued and interested in this series after having read the synopsis. The second I picked up the book, I couldn't put it down. This book has basically everything that I'm looking for. Paranormal? Check. Good writing? Check. Good plot? Check. Awesome main character? Check. Hot guys? Check AND check. <br><br>The Storyline/Writing:<br>In the beginning I was a bit confused with all of the terminology. Along the way though, everything is explained. I really liked the "Past" and "Now" variation to the story. Instead of Nikki or someone else just telling a long story of the crucial events that took place before this book (which would be so boring), Ashton uses the past and present writing tool. It worked quite well and there were never instances where the switching between times was annoying. I equally loved both past and present scenes! The writing was descriptive and detailed. I loved the modern storytelling of Hades and Persephone aspect. <br><br>The Characters: <br>All of the characters in this book are so wonderful. They are realistic and emotional and act like actual human beings. No one is perfect. No one is too outlandishly damaged. There's a certain realness to the characters. Nikki is a great main character. She is so funny and sweet and kind and smart. Her little brother is adorable. Jack and Cole. Wow. More on them later. <br><br>The Love Triangle:<br>Usually I don't really like love triangles. The only ones I like and appreciate are the strong love triangles where you have no idea who the main character will pick, and you love both of the guys. This is one of those books.<br>"Team Jack! Wait no, Team Cole!!! Wait but... Team Jack!! No Team Cole!!"<br>OK, I don't really know which team I am. I keep changing teams!! <br>Jack is such a wonderful person. He is so handsome and strong and gentle and caring and thoughtful. Cole is the hot bad boy with the arrogance and humor. How ever will I choose?<br><br>The Ending:<br>I really didn't see it coming. The whole book was fantastic, but the last 50 pages were phenomenal. I still can't believe that ending ;(<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389317473ra/8019616.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Things that I didn't like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389239092ra/8009458.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I highly recommend this book to YA readers!!<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7819428148036300204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_231908403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231908403" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1233686-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334791106p2/1233686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231908403?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1233686-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=nook-book">nook-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231908403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5045651208635243686"><i>Everneath</i> has some fantastic ideas which include Greek and Egyptian mythology, comparisons between otherworldly activity and drug addiction, and a bad boy who makes no excuses about being a bad boy. Unfortunately the book simply didn't deliver. Rather than a full length novel, <i>Everneath</i> reads as one very (very) long introduction to a novel. Go read the synopsis for this book...... Done? Well, no need to read the book now, because that is pretty much all that happens <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Except for th</span></span>
  <span id="freeText5045651208635243686" style="display:none"><i>Everneath</i> has some fantastic ideas which include Greek and Egyptian mythology, comparisons between otherworldly activity and drug addiction, and a bad boy who makes no excuses about being a bad boy. Unfortunately the book simply didn't deliver. Rather than a full length novel, <i>Everneath</i> reads as one very (very) long introduction to a novel. Go read the synopsis for this book...... Done? Well, no need to read the book now, because that is pretty much all that happens <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Except for the ending, Nikki manages to avoid getting sucked back into the Everneath. But, because this is YA PNR you already knew (or should have known!) that was going to happen  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Seriously, there is nothing which happened in this novel which wasn't stated in the synopsis. Sure, Nikki loves her father, brother and former boyfriend Jack. But if she has experienced any character development or poignant moments, I wouldn't know it. In fact, I don't know a thing about her character. Sure, she has feelings (because we are told about them over and over) and she is brave and selfless and would rather suffer herself than do harm to another person. *yawn* Let's see, the love interest Jack is also like totally good. The other love interest Cole seems to be like totally devoted to Nikki even though he isn't completely honest and does bad things. *yawn* This triangle is a proven formula, and although it embarrasses me to admit it, I am a big fan of the lurve triangle when properly done. Cole is interesting because he makes no apologies for what he is and does. But overall, Nikki, Jack and Cole are all so bland, so lifeless that I don't really care what becomes of them. There are a few secondary characters which could have made this novel more interesting had they been mentioned in more than passing; Nikki's dad, her brother, her bff Jules, that blonde cheerleader bitch *double yawn* <br /><br />We also do learn some rules and mythology regarding the Everneath but nothing especially captivating or worthy of keeping me on the edge of my seat. I can't help but feel Everneath has suffered from the current <s>trend</s> demand for series in YA. Again, nothing happens in this novel. Nothing. Had Ashton condensed her planned trilogy into one full length novel, it might have been really good. But as it is this is one painfully long introduction which simply isn't enticing enough to inspire me to continue.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5045651208635243686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10954680512875860087" style="display:none">Edit: SO SORRY THIS KEEPS POPPING UP! I just keep remembering little tid bits, and.... yeah:) <br /><br />May have spoilers??! Idk<br /><br />I can't believe I have gone from the amazingness of Eliza and Her Monsters to this.<br />It is suppose to be a Persephone and Hades retelling, but instead I just got a bunch of melodramatic, high school dating crap, with a slight hint at, story's said-Underworld. <br />So, yeah. This is a character driven book, and all of the characters are just petty, immature, and just no, no, no.<br /><br />Nikki, our MC, is annoying, uninteresting and has no frickin' backbone. <br />She also has no regard whatsoever for self-preservation, which is annoying as all get out!<br />No hobbies, no friends apparently, since she never goes into depth about said-best friend, Jules, and she gets flustered over the sight of a fucking piece of tongue jewelry! <br />Let me explain:<br />During her time "Before the Feed," she is apparently super-uber-duper in love with football player boyfriend, Jack (I know, he is just so unique *rolls fucking eyeballz*) and can't flippin' think straight and shit when they are together. Cue more of my eyeballz. BUT! Not even 2 pages later, she's getting hot in the face, cause she catches a glimpse of Cole's fucking tongue post!!!!<br />She also acts out like a complete child, when she gets upset and <b>throws</b>--I kid you not--her backpack at her dad's face. You sure you're seventeen? Maybe your memory is a bit muddled from all that time down in Everneath, even tho I GOT NO DETAILS OF THAT!!! Yeah. Totes norms.<br /><br />My other problem with Nikki is more aimed at the author. God! Every girl, besides Nik, is made out to seem like a brainless, boy-crazy-bitch. He just pisses me off. I mean he beat someone up, cause he overheard a boy call Nikki--not to antagonize or tease him-- that Nikki was a crackhead. GET YOUR FUCKING SHIT TOGETHER MAN!!! He tells Jack of how Nikki is gonna leave again, saying after words that Jack deserved to know, even tho he did it in the most obnoxious way possible! <br />Other than that tho, he somehow makes my heart go all achy-breaky..... stupid heart.... :(<br /><br />The characters are not the only part that is ridicules. No, it's also how toned down every sexual-ish thing is.<br /><br /><i>"Do you mean, are we. . ." He held up the index fingers of both his hands, and then put the tips together and made a loud smoochy noise.</i><br /><br />Oh, please. Everyone knows the sign for "together" isn't kissy fingers, it's "okay" sign, plus pointer finger. Also, when Cole gets asked to autograph things for fans (he is a musician. Great. Options are football brute, or musician. *MORE EYEBALL ACTION*) he signs "<i>even one girl's arm.</i>" No, "even" would be used for like the girl's boob or something XD!<br /><br />Anyways, after this ranty, thingamajigy, you'd think this would be like a 1 start rating, but no. It's 2 cuz this book is so damn addictive! I am only continuing the trilogy so I can get more heart flutteries from Cole *giggles hysterically* <br /><br />Okay, now I'm done! *jazz hands!*</span>

<div id="review_140603842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140603842" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140603842?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=whitneyawards">whitneyawards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140603842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5606048961772606299">Okay, so a few years back I critiqued some first pages at a writers' conference. There were a couple of stories that were fine but forgettable, some that were terrible, one that had so many made-up fantasy words that it might as well have been written in Finnish, and a cute little ten year old girl with quite a good alien abduction story. And then a lovely blonde in the corner of the room read her first pages, about a high school girl who's been missing for six months, and everyone assumes she's</span>
  <span id="freeText5606048961772606299" style="display:none">Okay, so a few years back I critiqued some first pages at a writers' conference. There were a couple of stories that were fine but forgettable, some that were terrible, one that had so many made-up fantasy words that it might as well have been written in Finnish, and a cute little ten year old girl with quite a good alien abduction story. And then a lovely blonde in the corner of the room read her first pages, about a high school girl who's been missing for six months, and everyone assumes she's on drugs when she reappears, gaunt and haunted . . . but in reality she's just spent a century in the underworld. GRIPPING! FASCINATING! ACTUALLY GOOD!<br /><br />Fast forward a couple of years and I meet Brodi Ashton through Bree Despain, and at a restaurant one night we start talking about that writers' conference, and I say, "Geez, I wish I knew what happened to that chick with the story about the girl serving time in hell." And Brodi goes, "Are you making fun of me?" Me: "No! Why?" Because that was her, the story was EVERNEATH, and she'd just gotten a contract for it. I was ecstatic for her!<br /><br />But could the rest of the book live up to the promise of those first pages? Why yes, yes it could. <br /><br />I LOVED this book! This was a creepy, fabulous twist on the myth of the underworld, mixing Persephone's story with Orpheus and Eurydice. Not only that, it was good YA. These were believable teens, talking in believable ways. There were enough details about school to make it seem real, without driving the reader crazy with minutiae. The bad guy really needed to be punched, repeatedly, about the head and genitals, and (this sounds horrible but its true) I loved how messed up Nikki was by her time in the Everneath. The little details about her hands shaking, and the way she just felt so fragile, were amazing. <br /><br />Now that paranormal romance has its own department at Barnes &amp; Noble, there are a lot of formulaic books out there. It's like, cue love triangle, cue reveal that he's a supernatural being, and begin trendy playlist! This is not one of those books, though. This is a real standout, with some VERY unexpected twists and some truly skillful writing.<br /><br />I can't wait for EVERBOUND!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5606048961772606299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_257289776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257289776" />
    <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan"><img alt="VampireNovelFan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296445543p2/4897902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257289776?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="VampireNovelFan" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan">VampireNovelFan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257289776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6046893545453654932"><a href='http://vampirenovelfan.wordpress.com/2012/01/14/everneath-forced-to-finish-this-one/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>Forced to finish this one</b>
</a><br/><br/>The cover suggests a slightly more mature theme, even within the YA genre. It can happen. I just finished reading a book where it happened. But 99% of the book is spent with her <em>outside</em> of this “Everneath”, resulting in a fairly uninteresting read. I read it quickly so I didn’t waste too much time on it, but I really don’t like it when covers are so deceptive.<br/><br/>Nikki is the central character of the story. 6 months ago she was taken to the Everneath by Cole, an immortal</span>
  <span id="freeText6046893545453654932" style="display:none"><a href="http://vampirenovelfan.wordpress.com/2012/01/14/everneath-forced-to-finish-this-one/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Forced to finish this one</b>
</a><br /><br />The cover suggests a slightly more mature theme, even within the YA genre. It can happen. I just finished reading a book where it happened. But 99% of the book is spent with her <em>outside</em> of this “Everneath”, resulting in a fairly uninteresting read. I read it quickly so I didn’t waste too much time on it, but I really don’t like it when covers are so deceptive.<br /><br />Nikki is the central character of the story. 6 months ago she was taken to the Everneath by Cole, an immortal who used her life force to sustain his own and his Queen’s. She spends 100 years literally attached to Cole as he feeds from her. Once the feeding is done it is discovered that Nikki is a unique case, surviving it as most others wouldn’t. This suggests that she has a special power, making her very attractive to Cole. She has a choice to stay in the Everneath with him, but she decides to go back home to be with her family and her boyfriend, Jack, who was her biggest motivation to remain alive. However, going back to the real world puts her on a countdown to destruction, destining her to spend an eternity in the Underworld. She tries to live her life (or what she has left of it) but Cole is an obvious interference, desperately trying to convince her to be with him and rule the Everneath. But her heart is with Jack, putting her in a predicament and forcing her to look for any alternative she can find. And therein lies the story.<br /><br />I didn’t really like how 100 years in the Everneath is only 6 months in the real world. That was too convenient. There is a lot of time jumping (showing POVs from past to present to past, etc. ) while counting down to the climax, but the build up isn’t intense. It’s very “day in the life”. The beginning ropes you in in hopes that you’re in for a super cool roller coaster ride, but then it turns into an unoriginal high school teen drama; I would have avoided this book had I known to expect that. In terms of characters, I preferred Cole simply because he was actually interesting and that was an actual challenge. Don’t get me wrong, he’s manipulative and a horrible love interest, but as a character I would have liked to have seen more. I like my villains to be more than one-dimensional. I started skimming the scenes with Jack after a while, though I got the point. This book was more teen romance with a dash of paranormal lore. Overall, if they took out the lore most of the book would be unaffected.<br /><br />The best parts were the brief mythology references. While it seems as if the next book could focus on a little more adventure, I’m not taking the bait. There are two other potentially interesting worlds that we merely hear about: the Everneath and the Underworld, and I wanted Nikki to explore both. This was the chance for the series to stand out to me and it didn’t. It’s got pretty good ratings overall though, so maybe it’s just me. I <i>might</i> be willing to read the second book if she does explore these worlds in future books, but I’m not waiting with bated breath for it.<br /><br />*ARC Provided by NetGalley</span>
  <a data-text-id="6046893545453654932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_269604413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269604413" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269604413?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269604413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16425171956392878619"><blockquote> It is easy to get a thousand prescriptions but hard to get one single remedy. -Chinese Proverb </blockquote><br/><br/> What drew me to Everneath was the Hades and Persephone myth that was incorporated into the story. Although the true gem of the story was finding one's feet after you feel your world has been destroyed. <br/> Nikki feels just like that, and ends up turning to the wrong person Cole. Next things she knows she’s been stuck into an underworld where immortals Feed on the emotions of those who have hit wrong bot</span>
  <span id="freeText16425171956392878619" style="display:none"><blockquote> It is easy to get a thousand prescriptions but hard to get one single remedy. -Chinese Proverb </blockquote><br><br> What drew me to Everneath was the Hades and Persephone myth that was incorporated into the story. Although the true gem of the story was finding one's feet after you feel your world has been destroyed. <br> Nikki feels just like that, and ends up turning to the wrong person Cole. Next things she knows she’s been stuck into an underworld where immortals Feed on the emotions of those who have hit wrong bottom like Nikki. Nikki though finds a way to get back to the surface and finally make her peace with her family and love ones before she’s suck back into the underworld. Only she can’t. Not when the feelings she thought were torn from her come back to her, and not when the love of her life- Jack- comes back into her life and gives her the strength to fight back in returning to Everneath and Cole.<br><br> Brodi Ashton added a little flavor of different myths while giving you the story from different points in time. This was very clever if not a tad slow in getting into the story. In the present Nikki counts down the days, weeks and months until she’s forced into returning to Everneath. To the past in how Nikki fell into this whole mess. Nikki isn’t a dumb, but heartbreaking sad as she find her way from heartbreak to trusting the world person to trying to make amends before she leaves again. I think everyone of us could understand where Nikki stood, dealing with depression, lost of a love one or just finally hitting the bottom. Might have chosen the wrong path in dealing with what she was going through, that wasn’t the point. It was having that someone who loved her, that anchor we all need in our life to help us dig ourselves out and be there for us like Jack is for Nikki. I loved Jack and all he stood for and his love for Nikki. He was true through and through and while sometimes it was a hard pill to see and learn about what had happen to Nikki he stood by her and loved her period.<br> The author deals very well with the subject of drugs in the form Cole and how he robs Nikki of her emotions. We can’t turn to drugs or someone to support us in a toxic way. And the author shows this with how Nikki is supported by her love ones and is able to overcome her “addiction” to Cole and dealing with the good and the bad.<br><br>The ending was heartbreaking and leaving the reader wanting more, but still with a great amount of hope that things will get better. Brodi Ashton created an amazing debut world with Everneath and the message of believing in ones self even when the odds are stacked against you and overcoming the odds. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368578ra/721176.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16425171956392878619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3393142400259267993">So for <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/389412-youngadultlovers-x1f338?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group'>https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/...</a> the book picked to read was... <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9413044.Everneath__Everneath___1_' title='Everneath (Everneath, #1) by Brodi Ashton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Everneath</a><br/>This book follows Nikki, who gave up her life on earth because of a broken heart, after a century of being locked up in the everneath,the underworld. She finally is allowed to spend 6 months to try and live her her life on earth and maybe reconnect with her boyfriend jack but there is also Cole, the boy who she spent a century with in the everneath and who cares about her deeply.<br/><br/>This book is on one my favroui</span>
  <span id="freeText3393142400259267993" style="display:none">So for <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/389412-youngadultlovers-x1f338?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group">https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/...</a> the book picked to read was... <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9413044.Everneath__Everneath___1_" title="Everneath (Everneath, #1) by Brodi Ashton" rel="nofollow noopener">Everneath</a><br />This book follows Nikki, who gave up her life on earth because of a broken heart, after a century of being locked up in the everneath,the underworld. She finally is allowed to spend 6 months to try and live her her life on earth and maybe reconnect with her boyfriend jack but there is also Cole, the boy who she spent a century with in the everneath and who cares about her deeply.<br /><br />This book is on one my favrouite books ever! Persephone and Hades is my favrouite myth and for someone that studies classics, this twist on the tale was beautifully written.<br />I loved how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4384465.Brodi_Ashton" title="Brodi Ashton" rel="nofollow noopener">Brodi Ashton</a> wrote the flashback and then the flash forwards.<br /><br />CHARACTERS-<br />Nikki is a very strong female protagonist, she knows what she wants and she goes out and gets it.<br />You really see her descions show who she is as a person.<br />Jack is my least favrouite character, I think in this book he dragged Nikki down. A lot of people adore jack in this book and I can understand why but he definitely not for me.<br />Cole is the most amazing character in this book, in my opinion and he will always be my favrouite. Cole honestly loves Nikki, and you could totally see that throughout the book. He would do anything for her and you see that by his speech and his actions.<br /><br />ROMANCE-<br />So everyone ships Jack and Nikki, but here I am Team Cole and Nikki.<br /> Jack isn't good for Nikki, like he drags her down and she has to make her descions based around him.<br />With Cole though, she has a witty strong relationship and you could really engage with them.<br /><br />WRITING-<br />The whole story was well-written and the mythology aspect was amazing.<br />This is such an under appreciated book and that really upsets me.</span>

<div id="review_199274904" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199274904" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199274904?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062120663" href="/book/show/13425406-everneath">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=2015-owned-challenge">2015-owned-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=i-should-know-better">i-should-know-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=hello-my-name-is-mary-sue">hello-my-name-is-mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=plot-what-plot">plot-what-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=i-whine-therefore-i-am">i-whine-therefore-i-am</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=romance-in-disguise">romance-in-disguise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199274904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12192107643914360449">Bullet Review:<br/><br/>I really shoulda known better. Other reviewers did indicate it was heavy on the romance, and unless the book is explicitly a romance novel, I hate romance.<br/><br/>DNF at 21%.<br/><br/>The whole book is about the various douche-bag boys that are in Nikki's life and how everything in her life revolves around them. I mean, her mom dies, but it's not her mother's death that makes her want to get rid of her emotions. Nope, it's a boy. As for returning to Earth after her exile in the Everneath? Same boy -</span>
  <span id="freeText12192107643914360449" style="display:none">Bullet Review:<br><br>I really shoulda known better. Other reviewers did indicate it was heavy on the romance, and unless the book is explicitly a romance novel, I hate romance.<br><br>DNF at 21%.<br><br>The whole book is about the various douche-bag boys that are in Nikki's life and how everything in her life revolves around them. I mean, her mom dies, but it's not her mother's death that makes her want to get rid of her emotions. Nope, it's a boy. As for returning to Earth after her exile in the Everneath? Same boy - not her brother or her dad. Nope, a boy.<br><br>Maybe if the characters had been noteworthy - but nope. The boys are a rainbow of d-baggery, girls constantly slut shame and hate on each other over boys, and our Mary Sue is about as interesting as a dishrag.<br><br>I regret buying this book in hardcover, but I am SO GLAD I never bought any of the sequels.<br><br>Full Review:<br><br>Nikki Beckett was living in Everneath but was given 6 months to live back on Earth. She does this for her boyfriend, Jack, who dumped her for some unknown reasons. He somehow is the reason she went to Everneath AND the reason she came back. (Logic? What is that?!) This book is about her wangsting over Jack and alternately being harassed by Cole, the man who deceived her into going into Everneath.<br><br>DNF at 21%.<br><br>I deserve a freaking @$$ medal for surviving the 21% that I did. But then I really ought to have known better. I read reviews stating that there was a heavy romantic element - maybe JUST a romance element - and it's my fault for not listening more to that.<br><br>It's not that I don't like romance. I do. One of my current favorite stories is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13642704.The_Mad_Scientist_s_Daughter" title="The Mad Scientist's Daughter by Cassandra Rose Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mad Scientist's Daughter</a>, and that has a big romantic element. I don't mind romance as a genre (though I don't read it very much), and I don't mind romance tied into another genre.<br><br>But as a rule, I tend to prefer it when if romance does appear in, say, urban fantasy, there is still urban fantasy. Or fantasy. Or science fiction.<br><br>Aw, hell, who am I fooling? Let's just be frank - the time for me liking sappy teenaged romances is long gone, particularly when the book is basically 90% teenaged sappy romance. There is, like I said above, nothing inherently wrong with romances, nor teenaged ones. Hell, lots of people LOVE sappy romances; hence why Nicholas Sparks is so wealthy.<br><br>But I don't like them. I like nuance in my romance or romantic-themed books. I like characters who can have a freakin' life outside of which sausage they are going to bone (hence my problem with Anita Blake). I like characters whose thoughts are more than about a boy's marbled abs (hence my problem with Bella Swan). I like characters who aren't constantly depressed and emo (hence my problem with Luce from "Fallen"). And most certainly, I like it when characters fall in love with someone who isn't a complete waste of oxygen (hence my problem with Nora from "Hush, Hush").<br><br>"Everneath" checks all the boxes in the Stereotypical Young Adult Genre.<br><br>Spineless female character who falls in pantslove with two boys who behave like monsters to her (admittedly, NOT on the scale of Patch from "Hush, Hush", but really, that takes incredible skill to write that awful of a hero). Lipservice to her Speshul Snowflake status. Angst. High School Drama.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427212982i/14248543.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've spent YEARS wading through shitty books, basically not reading or hating to read because of books like this. I'm DONE. NO MORE. I refuse to continue reading - or listening on audiobook - anything that is not entertaining me.<br><br>Perhaps the book does a 180 and suddenly becomes amazing. Perhaps I truly am an old, grumpy hag with too much time on her hands. Perhaps I don't "get" the amazing-ness of the young adult genre, reading endless books where the characters are the same but with different names in different high schools. So what? I'm not happy with the book, and I won't lie.<br><br>Now, maybe these sorts of things are right up your alley. Maybe you LOVE teenaged romances, slightly on the sappy side. GOOD FOR YOU. Really. No sarcasm. I'm happy you like it. But as for me, nope, I'm all done.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403712884ra/10133996.gif" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12192107643914360449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
